<div id="review_2320896304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320896304" />
    <a title="Amanda || eastofreaden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7739224-amanda-eastofreaden"><img alt="Amanda || eastofreaden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530209798p2/7739224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320896304?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda || eastofreaden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda || eastofreaden" href="/user/show/7739224-amanda-eastofreaden">Amanda || eastofreaden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7739224-amanda-eastofreaden?shelf=gilmore-girls">gilmore-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7739224-amanda-eastofreaden?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320896304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4188796536614251633"><blockquote>
  <i>It always stimulates me to discover new examples of my own prejudice and stupidity, to realize that I don't know half as much as I think I do.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Several months deep into his recovery from a near-fatal illness, Sydney Orr discovers a new stationery shop where he buys a blue notebook. It's September 18, 1982, and over the next 9 days, this notebook completely absorbs Sydney's mind. He is unable to escape a world of cryptic premonitions and unnerving events that threaten his marriage and trust in </span>
  <span id="freeText4188796536614251633" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>It always stimulates me to discover new examples of my own prejudice and stupidity, to realize that I don't know half as much as I think I do.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Several months deep into his recovery from a near-fatal illness, Sydney Orr discovers a new stationery shop where he buys a blue notebook. It's September 18, 1982, and over the next 9 days, this notebook completely absorbs Sydney's mind. He is unable to escape a world of cryptic premonitions and unnerving events that threaten his marriage and trust in reality.<br /><br />There is something about Auster that I just really love. He takes regular ongoings, things that some would call mundane, and is able to put a spin on them that keeps you completely hooked. There is always something sinister and brooding beneath the surface, though, and I think that's something that requires a delicate hand to do well. But along with that, this story had a lot of love and heart.<br /><br />This is my third Auster, and I'm definitely learning his trademarks. It can be a little random. There is a point where it seems like he may have possibly gone off the tracks, but then it comes around and makes sense. I love the way he writes a story-within-a-story (and in this case, add another story). I even found his footnotes to be a perfect addition to the stories. I tend to find this pretentious when authors add these to their work when it's fiction, but I loved it.<br /><br />I look forward to exploring more of Auster's work. I can't wait to see who else he introduces me to, and what other stories I get pulled into.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4188796536614251633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_350296755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350296755" />
    <a title="Ricardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9861143-ricardo"><img alt="Ricardo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590147925p2/9861143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350296755?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricardo" href="/user/show/9861143-ricardo">Ricardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/96059.Oracle_Night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9861143-ricardo?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350296755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14195675303398998357">Magnificent! <br/><br/>Auster at his best. Starts off slowly and it takes around 50 pages to get into the novel (only reason it's not rated with 5 stars) but then it gathers pace and what unravels is a all encompassing novel that, despite its shortness, possesses great depth. Auster juggles so many themes and stories that he sends the reader to a state of nausea and confusion until, like a mighty ubiquitous author, everything is suddenly iluminated in front of our eyes. <br/><br/>This novel challenges our perceptio</span>
  <span id="freeText14195675303398998357" style="display:none">Magnificent! <br /><br />Auster at his best. Starts off slowly and it takes around 50 pages to get into the novel (only reason it's not rated with 5 stars) but then it gathers pace and what unravels is a all encompassing novel that, despite its shortness, possesses great depth. Auster juggles so many themes and stories that he sends the reader to a state of nausea and confusion until, like a mighty ubiquitous author, everything is suddenly iluminated in front of our eyes. <br /><br />This novel challenges our perception(s) of reality and blurrs the line between genres. Part ghost-story without any ghosts, the novel is addictive, moving, extremely well crafted. <br /><br />The best way of describing the novel is to quote John Trause, one of the main characters: 'Words are real. Everything human is real, and sometimes we know things before they happen, even if we aren't aware of it. We live in the present, but the future is inside us at every moment.' </span>
  <a data-text-id="14195675303398998357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2533134238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2954567996469608204">A story within a story, within a story, within ten more stories. I love Paul Auster, but I think this will be my forever favourite of his. At times this week I felt addicted to this book, and I often chose it over Netflix. Auster uses footnotes in his story-telling in a way that make this piece of literary fiction as post-modern as it is old-fashioned. It’s scatty and unfocused in plot, which I loved and was frustrated by in equal measure. But then the inside of a writer’s head (and by extension</span>
  <span id="freeText2954567996469608204" style="display:none">A story within a story, within a story, within ten more stories. I love Paul Auster, but I think this will be my forever favourite of his. At times this week I felt addicted to this book, and I often chose it over Netflix. Auster uses footnotes in his story-telling in a way that make this piece of literary fiction as post-modern as it is old-fashioned. It’s scatty and unfocused in plot, which I loved and was frustrated by in equal measure. But then the inside of a writer’s head (and by extension, his lead character, also a writer) is nothing if not scatty, lovable and frustrating.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lRvPTceXnPrKeDJmN9Snb5fyVtuswPjHCygNQUxKZBuycQHbjv4XIWGoi7VESLgULm50922YtvaDoOK7wQ2/Mw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1OLVj8pyds62qSSKDtiiCyemUbgloyIOA/F1Yf0keTrziBsZgxv9FR15nVl9RL1wnjpzlOT7bD+LeZqbcGOiEg==')})
  }

En la primera parte, se describe el funcio<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7208391140856938384\" style=\"display:none\">La acción de El matadero se sitúa en la década de 1830, durante la dictadura de Juan Manuel Rosas en Argentina y ha de entenderse la concepción y el objetivo primero de este texto como un ataque al dictador. En la primera parte, se describe el funcionamiento de un matadero de reses con una sucesión de cuadros realistas protagonizados por todos aquellos involucrados directa e indirectamente en las faenas, desde los perros olisqueros hasta el recaudador de impuestos, pasando por los hambrientos y rapaces niños y los crueles carniceros. En la segunda describe la situación de Buenos Aires durante la tiranía rosista y la infausta actuación de La Mazorca, la banda de asesinos a su servicio. La intención del autor de darle a Buenos Aires la connotación de matadero es patente; las escenas sangrientas se repiten de igual manera tanto al interior de éste como en las calles de la ciudad. Además de su carácter coyuntural, la narración posee una innegable importancia en la historia de la literatura por cuanto aparece como precursora (por su concepción, desarrollo y forma), del naturalismo y el realismo que posteriormente se desarrollaría en Europa.\n\nLa cautiva, hace parte de la obra en verso Rimas, publicada en 1837. En ella se describe la epopeya de la colonización de las pampas habitadas por indígenas que defendieron con valor sus tierras de la invasión de los colonos. El autor no pretende con este texto apoyar al aborigen; al contrario, considera al blanco poseedor de un derecho natural sobre la posesión de la tierra. Pero su descripción de los paisajes infinitos de la pampa es apenas comparable con la historia de amor y de heroísmo que desarrolla a lo largo de la obra.<\/span>\n  <a <span id="freeTextContainer13851085642762027399">Paul Auster is the bestselling author of <em>Report from the Interior</em>, <em>Winter Journal</em>, <em>Sunset Park</em>, Invisible, <em>The Book of Illusions</em>, and <em>The New York Trilogy</em>, among many other works. He has been awarded the Prince of Asturias Prize for Literature, the Prix Médicis Étranger, the Independent Spirit Award, and the Premio Napoli. He is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters, the American Ac</span>
  <span id="freeText13851085642762027399" style="display:none">Paul Auster is the bestselling author of <em>Report from the Interior</em>, <em>Winter Journal</em>, <em>Sunset Park</em>, Invisible, <em>The Book of Illusions</em>, and <em>The New York Trilogy</em>, among many other works. He has been awarded the Prince of Asturias Prize for Literature, the Prix Médicis Étranger, the Independent Spirit Award, and the Premio Napoli. He is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters, the American Academy of Arts and Sciences, and a Commandeur de l'Ordre des Arts et des Lettres. He lives in Brooklyn, New York.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13851085642762027399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
